1,413' FEL & 1,232' FSL

Lost Bridge Field / Three Forks
Dunn County, North Dakota
BOTTOM HOLE LOCATION:
11,543.19' south & 786.80' east of surface location or approx.
205.43' FSL & 626.20' FEL; SE SE Section 24, T148N, R96W
Prepared for:

WELL EVALUATION
Marathon Oil Company
Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH
Figure 1. H&P Rig #259 drilling the Marathon Oil Company, Gulbrand 44-12TFH
well in Dunn County, North Dakota during November of 2014. (Anna Bruckmeier, Geologist)
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company - Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH well lies within Lost Bridge Field and
is located approximately 21 miles north of Killdeer, North Dakota in Dunn County [SW SE
Section 12, T148N, R96W]. Lost Bridge Field has historically produced 365,204 barrels of oil
from Devonian formations, and 5,329,108 barrels of oil from the Bakken. The Gulbrand USA
44-12TFH is the fourth of four wells completed on this pad by H&P #259 for Marathon Oil
Company (Figure 1). The Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH is a double-section, horizontal well drilled to
the south (176.10°) within the Three Forks Formation. The vertical was planned to be drilled to a
kick-off point of 10,650' MD within the Lodgepole Formation. Build rates of 12° per 100' were
required to land the curve at approximately 90° within the targeted interval, 28' below the base
of the Lower Bakken Shale. Intermediate casing would then be set and cemented prior to
commencing the lateral portion of the well. The lateral would be drilled to a planned total depth
of 22,551' MD within the SE SE quadrant of Section 24, T148N, R96W. Upon the completion of
the well, the hole will be prepared for casing and production evaluation using staged artificial
fracture techniques.
OFFSET WELLS
Three primary offsets were used to establish a prognosis of formation tops and thicknesses to be
used as a control for the Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH (Figure 2). Offset formation thicknesses were
compared and an appropriate curve landing target was selected based on the average of these
thicknesses. The offset wells include:
-Victor USA 34-12TFH [SW SE Sec. 12, T148N, R96W] which shares the same pad as the
Victor USA 34-12TFH. It is a Middle Bakken horizontal that is currently active.
-Buffalo 34-12H [SW SE Sec. 12, T148N, R96W] which shares the same pad as the Gulbrand
USA 44-12TFH. It is a Three Forks horizontal that is currently active.
-Morean USA 34-12H [SW SE Sec. 12, T148N, R96W] which shares the same pad as the
Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH. It is a Three Forks horizontal that is currently active.
The Morean USA 34-12H was used for structure control and the Victor USA 34-12TFH was
used for gamma character through the lateral section.
Figure 2. Map showing the location of the Marathon Oil Company, Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH, and the locations of
the wells used for offset control and log character (NDIC Oil & Gas Division, Arc IMS online).
ENGINEERING
H&P rig #259 spud the Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH on October 19, 2014, with freshwater and a 12
¼" PDC bit, and drilled 2,247' in 4 drilling hours where a string of 9 5/8" surface casing was set
and cemented to a depth of 2,250' MD. The freshwater was then displaced with diesel invert
drilling mud, weighing 9.70-10.50 pounds/gallon, for the vertical and curve portions of the well.
Vertical operations were completed with three 8 ¾" PDC bits that drilled to a total depth of
10,650' MD. The vertical portion of the well was completed on October 26, 2014 at 03:00 CT
with three bits, totaling 8,295' in 76.5 drilling hours.
A fixed 2.38° mud motor and 8 ¾" PDC bit were tripped in the hole at 10,650' MD for the curve
build section. The curve was drilled to 10,996' MD where the decision was made to trip for a
new MWD tool and a more aggressive bit. An 8 ¾ tri-cone bit and adjustable 3.00° mud motor
were then tripped in the hole. Curve build continued to 11,127' MD where slides were not
yielding proper build rates, and the decision was made to trip again for a less aggressive bit. An
8 ¾" PDC bit and 3.00° adjustable mud motor were tripped in the hole. The curve was drilled to
a total depth of 11,670' MD at 10:25 CT on October 29, 2014. The 1,020' resultant curve was
drilled in 25.4 drilling hours. Seven inch, intermediate casing was set to a depth of 11,670' MD
and cemented.
Diesel invert drilling fluid was displaced with saltwater for the duration of the lateral with a
density of 9.80-9.90 pounds/gallon. Lateral operations began on November 1, 2014, at a depth
of 11,670' MD with a 6" PDC bit, 1.5° fixed bend mud motor, and Scientific MWD tools. After
drilling 1,337' in 17.1 drilling hours, to a depth of 13,007' MD, the decision was made to trip out
of the hole for a new bit due to low drilling rates. The new assembly drilled 5,892', to 18,899'
MD, in 44.1 drilling hours before the decision was made to trip out of hole for a new bit and
motor. The final assembly drilled 3,581', to 22,480' MD in 25.3 drilling hours, where total
depth was reached on November 8, 2014 at 09:05 CT with a closure azimuth of 176.10° and a
closure distance of 11,569.97'. The bottom-hole location is estimated to be 11,543.19' south and
786.80' east of surface location or approximately 205.20' FSL & 626.20' FEL, SE SE Section 24,
T148N, R96W in Dunn County, North Dakota (Figure 3).
Figure 3. Plan view of Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH spacing unit and well path as drilled.
GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
Sunburst Consulting, Inc. provided well-site geologic supervision for the Gulbrand USA 44-
12TFH. Two, two-person teams of geologists provided geo-steering services as well as logged
cuttings and monitored gas from 8,700 until the well was drilled to completion. A digital gas
detection system and chromatograph provided by Mudlogging Systems, Inc. were interfaced
with the Pason electronic data recording system (EDR), which provided drilling parameters to
the MControl program as well as displayed total gas data accessible around location. Total mud
gas data were measured and recorded in units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air) and
measured component concentrations of methane, ethane, propane, and butane in parts per
million. Rock cuttings were collected by rig crews in 30' lagged samples under the supervision
of the well site geologists. The cuttings were then examined wet and dry using a 10x-35x zoom
binocular stereo microscope with 10x oculars. These data, in conjunction with gamma ray data
provided by the Scientific MWDs and real-time drilling parameters from the Pason EDR, were
used to provide the directional team with optimal TVD targets ensuring the well-bore would
achieve maximum contact within the targeted drilling interval.
Prospective Pay Zones and Hydrocarbon Shows
Note: There were no electric logs run for the Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH; therefore, all depths
while drilling the vertical and curve are referenced to driller's depth. A complete listing of
sample descriptions is provided in the appendix of this report.
The Mission Canyon Formation [Mississippian; Madison Group] was present at 9,663' MD
[9,660 TVD, (-7,143' subsea)]. The Mission Canyon is characterized by a transition from
argillaceous and dolomitic limestone to clean limestone. The lithology of the Mission Canyon is
comprised of several interbeds of anhydrite, dolomite and limestone. Samples consisted
primarily of mudstone that was light gray to light brown in color and occasionally argillaceous.
Trace amounts of intercrystalline porosity and dark brown spotty oil staining were noted in the
middle and lower portions of the formation which were accompanied by hydrocarbon shows of
83 units (9,940' MD), 172 units (10,194') MD) and 162 units (10,120'MD) and background gas
averaging between 50 and 60 units.
The Lodgepole Formation [Mississippian; Madison Group] was encountered at 10,222' MD
[10,214' TVD (-7,697' subsea)] and marked by a transition from clean limestone to argillaceous
limestone; predominately mudstone. Samples were primarily gray-brown in color with trace
amounts of disseminated pyrite and no visible porosity or oil staining observed. There was one
significant hydrocarbon show, most likely a result of fracture porosity, seen at 11,144' MD,
reaching 694 units. Background gas averaged between 20 and 40 units overall, and increased to
300 units at the base of the formation. Three trip gasses were observed in the Lodgepole, the first
at 10,650' MD reaching 107 units, the second at 10,996' MD reaching 244 units, and the third at
11,127' MD reaching 157 units. The lower 20' of the Lodgepole is characterized by two
informal sub-intervals: the False Bakken and the underlying Scallion interval. The False Bakken
is a dark gray calcareous shale that yielded a 427 unit hydrocarbon show. The Scallion is a gray
to brown limestone with no visible intercrystalline, but indicated frequent fracture porosity by
the amount of total gas derived through this interval.
The Upper Shale Member of the Bakken Formation [Mississippian] was logged at 11,217' MD
[11,093' TVD (-8,576' subsea)] with sample returns consisting of hard, black, carbonaceous and
petroliferous shale with common disseminated and nodular pyrite. The penetration of the shale
was accompanied by a higher gamma signature, faster drilling rates, and increased hydrocarbon
shows-specifically a show of 3,287 units at 11,221' MD and 2,276 units at 11,272' MD. The
Middle Bakken Member [Devonian-Mississippian] was logged at 11,276' MD [11,114' TVD
(-8,597' subsea)] with sample returns consisting of light gray-brown, very fine grained, silty
sandstone that is calcite and occasionally dolomite cemented and has trace amounts of
disseminated pyrite. The upper portion of the Middle Bakken is characterized by a gray,
calcareous, siltstone underlain by a thin layer of packstone, noted by a significant decrease in
gamma values. Trace amounts of intergranular porosity and light brown spotty oil staining were
observed and accompanied by a hydrocarbon show of 789 units at 11,311' MD. Background gas
averaged between 400 and 600 units for the duration of this interval. The Lower Shale Member
was logged at 11,398' MD [11,155' TVD (-8,643' subsea)] with sample returns of dark brown to
black, carbonaceous and petroliferous shale similar to the upper member. It is also characterized
by faster drilling rates, higher gamma signature, and increased hydrocarbon shows as opposed to
the middle member. Background gas averaged around 1,000 units, with a show of 1,719 units at
11,413' MD. The Pronghorn Member [Devonian] was reached at 11,482' MD [11,182' TVD (-
8,665' subsea) and is characterized by dark gray shale, siltstone and light gray-brown limestone.
Rare to occasional amounts of disseminated and nodular pyrite were also observed. Light brown
spotty oil staining was accompanied by a 940 unit hydrocarbon show at 11,526' MD.
The Three Forks Formation [Devonian] was logged at 11,530' MD [11,192' TVD (-
8,675'subsea)] with sample returns of pale green shale, off white and light brown sandy dolomite
and trace amounts of a light gray dolomite cemented sandstone. Pyrite is seen throughout the
upper Three Forks, most commonly in euhedral form in the shale and occasionally as
disseminated and nodular in the shale and dolomite. No visible porosity was observed in the
shale intervals. Rare spotty to even oil staining and intercrystalline porosity were both observed
in the dolomite intervals. The targeted zone was 12' thick and described as (Figure 4):
DOLOMITE: mudstone, off white to light brown, microcrystalline, friable to firm, sucrosic
texture, sandy in part, trace to rare disseminated pyrite, trace intercrystalline porosity,
rare spotty to even dark brown oil stain; occasional SHALE: pale green, firm, earthy
texture, rare to occasional euhedral pyrite, trace disseminated pyrite
Figure 4. Shale and sandy dolomite from the targeted interval. (Anna Bruckmeier, Well-site Geologist)
Geo-steering
Day tour directional services and well-site supervision were provided by Pat's Consulting and
Scientific Drilling International provided night directional and MWD services throughout the
duration of the well. Sunburst Consulting, Inc. well-site geologists worked in conjunction with
the directional drillers, MWDs, and the prospect geologist to make decisions ensuring maximum
well-bore exposure within the targeted zone.
The prognosis called for a landing target of 11,226' TVD, 33' below the base of the lower
Bakken shale, placing the well-bore in the center of target at approximately 90°. Real time
gamma data obtained from the MWDs was used to correlate formation thicknesses between the
Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH and its offsets. While drilling the vertical and the curve, the landing
target was changed to 11,210' TVD after correlating real time gamma-ray from the "Base of Last
Salt", Lodgepole markers, and False Bakken, in comparison to the previously drilled Morean
USA 34-12H offset well. The actual landing was at 11,207' TVD, putting the well-bore right at
the top of the 12' target, entering the target zone at 11,654' MD. The top of the 12' target came
in at 11,207' TVD and the bottom of the target came in at 11,219' TVD.
Gamma-ray readings crossing through the top of the 12' target (marker C) were typically around
60-85 (API) respectively, 60-110 (API) through the center (marker D), and 40-110 (API) through
the base and below (marker F-marker H). Real time MWD gamma-ray signatures correlated
well with the gamma data from the Victor USA 32-12TFH offset well (Figure 5).
Figure 5. Type log (left) and the Victor USA 32-12TFH MWD gamma log (right, in green) that were used to provide
correlation for the subject well (See Figure 6).
Transitions from high to low gamma-ray markers, and amplitude of gamma counts provided
comparative points from which dip estimates and steering decisions were made. Gas readings
and sample observations also helped make dip estimates by determining the position of the well-
bore within the stratigraphic interval. Offset wells also contributed to excellent structure control,
since the Morean USA 34-12H well paralleled the subject well directly to the west. Structure
trends during the first half of the lateral were downwards ranging from 0.12º - 2.89º then, due to
a plunging synclinal structure, the structure immediately came back up ranging from 0.31 ­
1.97º.
The second half of the lateral remained fairly flat, decreasing slightly by 0.20º then
increasing towards the end to 0.30º. The formation dropped 6', over 10,826', resulting in a gross
apparent down-dip of 0.03° observed upon completion of the lateral.
The well-bore drilled below the target interval on three occasions, coming down into the
chocolate shale, totaling approximately 3,340' and above the target interval on two occasions
totaling approximately 1,040'. The majority of the lateral was drilled within the center of the
target interval and below. Steering was successful in maintaining the well-bore in the desired
target interval for approximately 60% of the 10,826' lateral section (Figure 6).

Figure 6. Profile illustrating the gamma-ray markers and dip estimates for the Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH .
Lateral Hydrocarbon Shows
Lateral hydrocarbon shows were highest in the lower half of zone, particularly between the base
of target and the chocolate dolomite, most likely due to the predominately sandy dolomite layer
just below the base of zone. Due to increasing connection gasses and a trip gas of 2,044 units,
the decision was made to begin circulating through the gas buster at 18,889' MD. Prior to that,
background gas averaged 300 units and increased to 800 units with connection gasses
approaching 1,800 and 2,400 units just before circulation through the gas buster began (Figure 7).
A continutous flare of 2-4' was observed from 18,900' MD to total depth. Gas components C1-
C4 were observed throughout the course of the lateral. Once circulation through the gas buster
began, average background gas dropped to 150-200 units with connection gasses averaging
between 300 and 450 units. No back pressure was held while drilling the Gulbrand USA 44-
12TFH.

Figure 7. Profile illustrating the gamma-ray markers, dip estimates, total gas and rate of penetration for the
Marathon Oil Company, Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH .
SUMMARY
The Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH is a Three Forks horizontal well successfully drilled in Lost
Bridge Field in 20 days, reaching a total depth of 22,480' on November 8, 2014. Samples from
the target zone consisted of pale green shale, an off white to light brown sandy dolomite with
sucrosic texture and spotty to even oil staining and trace amounts of a light gray dolomite
cemented sandstone, all with varying abundances of pyrite. Background gas values were 300-
800 units during the first portion of the lateral and decreased to 150-200 units once circulation
through the gas buster began. A flare of 2-4' was observed throughout the lateral. No back
pressure was held. The overall apparent dip was approximately 0.03° down. The well-bore
remained in the target zone for 60% of the lateral, exposing 6,446' to the pay zone.
The
Marathon Oil Company, Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH will be fitted with 4½" production liner in
preparation for a multi-staged fracture stimulation that will determine the true commercial value
of the well and currently awaits completion.
Respectfully submitted,
Matthew Kidd
Anna Bruckmeier
Danielle Haydal
Well-site geologist
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
Marathon Oil Company ­ Gulbrand USA 44-12TFH
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A detailed list of
sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma ray marker tops have been inserted
in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope.
The drilling fluid was diesel-based invert from surface casing to 11,670' and changed to salt-water from 11,670' to
22,480' TD. Sample collection began at 8,700'.
Drilling in the Kibbey Formation: Kibbey "Lime"
8,704' MD; 8,697' TVD (-6,180')
8700-8730 SILTY SANDSTONE: light brown, light to medium gray, occasional red to brown, firm, sub-blocky,
calcite cemented, poorly cemented, occasional ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, firm to soft, massive, amorphous
8730-8760 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown, microcrystalline, firm to friable, earthy texture;
SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, light brown, occasional light red to brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented,
poorly cemented
8760-8790 SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, light red-brown, light orange-brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite
cemented, poorly cemented
8790-8820 SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, light red-brown, light orange-brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite
cemented, poorly cemented
8820-8850 SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, light red-brown, light orange-brown, firm, sub-blocky, calcite
cemented, poorly cemented

3172 Hwy 22 N

RE:
HORIZONTAL WELL
GULBRAND USA 44-12TFH
SWSE Section 12-148N-96W
Dunn County
Well File # 29004
Dear William:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24318, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is granted on
the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback from the north & south
boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 1,12,13&24 T148N
R96W. Tool error is not required pursuant to order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must
be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and
flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required
surrounding the entire location. All distances on the Production Layout Plat must comply with NDAC 43-02-03-28 (SAFETY
REGULATION). MARATHON OIL COMPANY must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) when
contemplating simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation)
"No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any producing well or oil tank."
MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Joyce Kohut at 701-202-1288 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and completion
operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of the land surface and
freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized
representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director
prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The proposed directional
plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 11550'S and
913'E.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved drilling permit
on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd business day following
publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn
affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and
any other information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit,
the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given immediately upon the
spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information
must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding.
Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
William F Groffy
July 30, 2014
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a certified
copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or
in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the
survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one
adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when sliding) and 90
feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby granted. Such
information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records wherever located.
Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the Director and his representatives to come
upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and
operation of such wells and to have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The
information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission and
its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail cement
utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and porosity zones
can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and (3) a log from which the
presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation log) in every well in which production
or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as
one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a
standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 150 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture
